GENERAL PROVISIONS AND ADMINISTRATION
§ 51.01 PUBLIC POLICY DECLARED.
   (A)   It is declared to be in the best interest of the public policy of the
town that there be a “Comprehensive Refuse Collection Ordinance” so that all
residents of the town will receive the benefit of trash collection and that all
residents of the town be responsible for such a service.
   (B)   By doing so, the town wishes to be able to bid competitively for such
services, thereby reducing the overall rate paid by each resident.
(Ord. 96-10, passed 7-7-1997)
§ 51.02 AWARDING GARBAGE COLLECTION CONTRACT.
   In order to achieve the lowest price for said services, the town shall
advertise for bids from contractors based upon a three-year contract for said
services. The bidding process is to comply with the regulations in the State
Code for municipalities.
(Ord. 96-10, passed 7-7-1997)
§ 51.03 “RESIDENT” EXPLAINED.
   (A)   All houses with an attached apartment or separate dwelling shall be
considered a resident for purposes of this chapter and shall be billed under
such as a resident of the town.
   (B)   A business where the owners live above in the same building shall be
considered a resident for purposes of this chapter and shall be billed under
such as a resident of the town.
   (C)   The residents of the trailer court in town shall be billed
individually for the trash collection.
   (D)   Included in such billing shall be churches, the town park, municipal
or town buildings and downtown containers, all within the town limits. Said
sites shall be considered a resident for purposes of this chapter and shall be
billed under such as a resident of the town.
(Ord. 97-07, passed 8-4-1997)
RATES AND BILLING
§ 51.15 BILLING FOR GARBAGE COLLECTION.
   After the contract is awarded, the town will be billed the entire yearly
amount for said refuse collection on a per rata basis each month. Said amount
will be divided equally between all residents of the town who currently receive
town water and/or town sewage, and each resident will be billed monthly along
with the water and sewage bills for his or her share of said bill. Said bills
for refuse collection shall be due at the same time the water and/or sewage
bills are paid and shall be paid in the same manner.
(Ord. 96-10, passed 7-7-1997) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.16 RATE FOR GARBAGE DISPOSAL SERVICES.
   The rate charged to residents of the town for garbage disposal services was
raised to $11.06 per month, effective January 1, 2023. The town may consider an
increase in the rate charged to residents of the town at such time as any
change in the cost to the town is realized.
(Res. 2017-11, passed 12-4-2017)
§ 51.17 COLLECTION OF FUNDS.
   The Clerk-Treasurer of the town is hereby authorized to collect said funds
stated above for each resident’s share of the refuse collection contract and
shall deposit said sums into the Refuse Fund for the town. In addition, the
Clerk-Treasurer is hereby authorized to promptly pay all appropriate monthly
sums due directly to the refuse collector according to the town contract.
(Ord. 96-10, passed 7-7-1997)
REGULATIONS FOR COLLECTION AND STORAGE
§ 51.30 RESTRICTIONS FOR SETTING OUT, STORING GARBAGE; DEFENSE.
   (A)   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      SCHEDULED TRASH PICKUP DAY. The day of the week on which the residents of
the town are scheduled by the trash disposal service for removal of trash from
the trash toters.
      TRASH TOTER. The container supplied by the trash disposal service for
residents to utilize for trash pickup, or any other container in which trash is
placed within with the intent that the trash pickup service will remove and
properly dispose of the trash.
   (B)   (1)   (a)   No person, firm, organization or corporation shall permit
a trash toter, trash, garbage or other discarded large items to be left in
plain view within ten feet of a public street or in the area designated by the
town for trash pickup, except for the following time period:
            1.   From 4:00 p.m. on the evening prior to the scheduled trash
pickup day until 4:00 p.m. on the day following the scheduled trash pick up
day; and
            2.   Large items shall not be left at the curb more than 24 hours
prior to the scheduled pickup day, which is presently the first Thursday of the
month.
         (b)   For purposes of this division (A), the fact that a trash toter
or other discarded material is found within 10 feet of a public street on real
estate owned by a person, except within the designated time period, is prima
facie evidence that the owner of such real estate is in violation of this
section.
      (2)   No person, firm, organization or corporation which is a resident of
the town shall leave or store a trash toter, trash, garbage or other discarded
items to be left in plain view within ten feet of a public street or in the
area designated by the town for trash pick up, except for the following time
period: from 4:00 p.m. on the evening prior to the scheduled trash pickup day
until 4:00 p.m. on the day following the scheduled trash pickup day.
      (3)   It is a defense to this section if the trash toter in question:
         (a)   Is stored within three feet of the residence; or
         (b)   If the trash toter is stored as far as practical from the
street.
      (4)   This section applies to residents of the town. Specifically, it is
a defense to the section if the trash toter is being utilized by the town or
any other tax exempt organization for a special event which is approved by the
Town Council.
(Ord. 2016-13, passed 2-6-2017) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.31 COLLECTION TO BE FROM CURB; EXCLUSIONS.
   (A)   The contractor awarded the job will make weekly collections of garbage
and rubbish from the curb line of each residence within the town. Any multi-
unit dwellings and businesses, including apartment complexes, shall be excluded
under this section.
   (B)   Only garbage and refuse will be collected at the curbside. The removal
of any furniture, appliances, construction debris and remodeling trash will not
be included in this chapter and will need to be specifically scheduled for
pickup directly with the refuse collector.
(Ord. 96-10, passed 7-7-1997)
§ 51.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   Any resident of the town who fails to promptly pay his or her bill for
the refuse collection, as set out under §
51.15 of this chapter, shall have a penalty of 10% of the refuse collection fee
that is imposed if not paid in full by the fifteenth of each month. Said
payments, or lack thereof, shall be monitored by the Clerk-Treasurer of the
town.
   (C)   (1)   Any person, firm, or organization found to be in violation of §
51.30 of this chapter shall be fined in an amount up to $50.
      (2)   Each day a person, firm or organization continues to remain in
violation of §
51.30 of this chapter is a separate offense.
(Ord. 96-10, passed 7-7-1997; Ord. 2016-13, passed 2-6-2017)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 52.01 WATER SERVICE PROVIDED WITHIN CORPORATE LIMITS.
   (A)   The town shall extend basic residential water service to any platted
lots within the corporate town limit which were platted prior to October
21,1997 where a building permit has been issued for the purpose of providing
water service to a residence. Said service shall be extended to the closest
part of the property line of the existing platted lot.
   (B)   Any expenses to take the water service from the property line to the
residence shall be borne by the home owner or developer. All connection and tap
fees shall still be applicable and shall not be affected by this section.
(Ord. 97-13, passed 11-3-1997)
§ 52.02 TAPPING FEE.
   Each user, at the time he or she is connected with the waterworks system,
shall pay a tapping fee to cover the cost of tapping the main, furnishing and
laying service pipe, service and meter box and installing the meter at the cost
of $500, plus cost of materials. In the event that boring under any street is
required for installation, the cost of said boring shall be paid by the user.
(Ord. 2000-5, passed 10-2-2000)
§ 52.03 METER DEPOSIT FEE.
   Meter deposits, beginning on November 1, 2000, and thereafter, shall be in
the amount of $125, and all customers applying for new service or change of
location on and after said date shall be required to maintain on deposit with
the town the sum of $125 as security against unpaid bills for water service,
and said deposits shall not be refunded to the customers until all bills and
charges owing the town are paid in full.
(Res. 2000-8, passed 9-7-2000)
§ 52.04 UNCLAIMED METER DEPOSIT FEE AFTER SERVICE DISCONTINUED.
   (A)   Any meter deposit fee which is not claimed by the resident entitled to
claim said fee within six years of the date that water service is discontinued
shall be considered abandoned, and said fees shall be transferred to the Water
Cash Operating Fund. Said funds shall be considered the property of the town
and may be used at the discretion of the Town Council.
   (B)   Each resident of the town shall be given notice at the time water
service is discontinued that the remainder of the meter deposit will be
forfeited to the town if it is not claimed with six years. Each resident shall
provide a forwarding address for which the town can utilize to forward notice
of the refund of any remaining water meter deposit fee. The failure of the
resident to provide a forwarding address to the town within 30 days of the
discontinuation of water service shall constitute a per se forfeiture of said
water meter deposit.
(Ord. 2005-03, passed 7-5-2005)
§ 52.05 RECONNECTION FEE AFTER DISCONNECTION FOR NONPAYMENT.
   (A)   Payment of outstanding/delinquent bill.
      (1)   At such time that any individual shall request reinstatement of
water utility services for any address within the town, the Town Clerk-
Treasurer shall determine whether there is any outstanding or delinquent water
bill for such address or residence.
      (2)   In the event that the Town Clerk-Treasurer determines that there is
a delinquent water bill for prior water utility services rendered at such
address or residence, any prior outstanding and/or delinquent water bill shall
be paid prior to the time that water utility service may be reconnected at such
address.
   (B)   Reconnection fee. Pursuant to Res. 2005-10, a reconnect fee of $35
shall be assessed against any user which has his or her water service
discontinued due to delinquent payment for water service provided by the town.
Said fee must be paid in full prior to the time that the water service will be
returned to said resident.
(Ord. 2009-04, passed 11-2-2009; Ord. 2021-03, passed 4-5-2021)
BILLING AND PAYMENT
§ 52.20 USE OF WATER EXPRESSES CONSENT TO CONTRACT.
   The water rates, rules and regulations herein provided for shall be
considered a part of the contract with each and every person, company or
corporation who is supplied with water by means of the water systems of the
town, and every person, company or corporation accepting water by said means
shall be considered to express his, hers or its consent to be bound thereby.
(Ord. 1982-10, passed 11-1-1982) Penalty, see §
52.99
§ 52.21 DEFERRED PAYMENT CHARGES.
   All bills for water service not paid within 15 days from the due date
thereof, as stated in such bills, shall be subject to the collection or
deferred payment charge of 10% on the first $3 and 3% on the excess over $3.
(Ord. 1982-10, passed 11-1-1982)
§ 52.22 FAILURE TO PAY.
   If payment for any water account is not made at the end of 30 days after
same account becomes due, the water furnished any customer may be shut off by
the town. All charges for water shall be paid by the property owner or owners,
and all such charges become a lien upon said property.
(Ord. 1960-1, passed - -) Penalty, see §
52.99
§ 52.23 PAYMENT BY RENTERS.
   Any property owner desiring to have his or her renters pay for water used
must give the town a written notice of such desire and a written statement that
such property owner will be responsible for the payment of any delinquent water
rent that might be owing by such renter or renters.
(Ord. 1960-1, passed - -) Penalty, see §
52.99
§ 52.24 CLERK-TREASURER TO COLLECT FUNDS, REPORT.
   The Town Clerk-Treasurer shall act as Clerk-Treasurer of the Town Municipal
Water Department, and he or she shall collect and receipt for all water rents
and place all money collected to the credit of the town, and her or she shall
report in writing to the Town Council, and at the first regular meeting in each
year, all receipts and disbursements of said Water Department. Whenever
permission of the town is required at any time the Town Council is not in
session, written permission of the Town Clerk- Treasurer shall be deemed
sufficient until such time as said Council shall meet and approve his or her
act and shall constitute full and complete permission when the records shall
show such approval, and all reports required to be made in writing to the Town
Council shall be deemed to be made when filed with the Clerk-Treasurer and
shall operate as a compliance with this section.
(Ord. 1960-1, passed - -)
§ 52.25 NOTICE OF DELINQUENCY.
   The Clerk-Treasurer shall mail notice of a water utility bill delinquency
exceeding 60 days to the owner of the real estate upon which the residence or
apartment is located. All owners of real estate located within the town shall
provide the Clerk-Treasurer of the town with a current mailing address. Any
property owner who fails to provide the town with a current mailing address
waives the notice requirement provided in division (A) above.
(Ord. 2009-04, passed 11-2-2009)
§ 52.26 BILL ADJUSTMENT AFTER A WATER LEAK.
   (A)   If a water leak occurs, and after the leak is repaired, the Town
Clerk-Treasurer shall make certain adjustments to the customer’s water bill
after the leak is corrected according to the following formula to determine the
charge for the customer. Under said circumstances, the customer will be charged
three times the average usage rate plus one-half the difference between the
actual usage and the average usage rate times three, as determined above.
   (B)   If a water leak occurs, the customer will also be given credit on the
sewage bill as well, and the customer will only be charged, for that month in
which the leak occurred, the average sewage rate over the previous six months
instead of the rate incurred due to the water leak.
(Ord. 96-15, passed 2-3-1996)
CROSS-CONNECTIONS AND BACKFLOW
§ 52.40 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CROSS-CONNECTION. Any physical connection or arrangement between two
otherwise separate systems, one of which contains potable water from the town
water system and the other, water from a private source, water of unknown or
questionable safety or steam, gases or chemicals, whereby there may be a flow
from one system to the other, the direction of flow depending on the pressure
differential between the two systems.
(Ord. 2018-04, passed 5-7-2018)
§ 52.41 SCOPE OF PROVISIONS.
   This subchapter does not supersede the state’s Uniform Plumbing Code but is
supplementary to it.
(Ord. 2018-04, passed 5-7-2018)
§ 52.42 CROSS-CONNECTIONS PROHIBITED; EXCEPTION.
   (A)   No person, firm or corporation shall establish or permit to establish,
or maintain or permit to be maintained, any cross-connection.
   (B)   No interconnection shall be established whereby potable water from a
private, auxiliary or emergency water supply other than the regular public
water supply of the town may enter the supply or the distribution system of
said municipality unless such private, auxiliary or emergency water supply, and
the method of connection and use of such supply, shall have been approved by
the Town Council and the Environmental Board of the state.
(Ord. 2018-04, passed 5-7-2018) Penalty, see §
52.99
§ 52.43 INSPECTIONS; RIGHT TO ENTER.
   (A)   (1)   It shall be the duty of the town water utility to cause
inspections to be made of all properties served by the public water system
where cross-connection with the public water system is deemed possible.
      (2)   The frequency of inspections and reinspections, based on potential
health hazards involved, shall be as established by the town water utility.
   (B)   (1)   Upon presentation of credentials, the representative of the town
waterworks shall have the right to request entry at any reasonable time to
examine the property served by a connection to the public water system of the
town for cross-connections.
      (2)   On request, the owner, lessee or occupant of any property so served
shall furnish to the inspection agency any pertinent information regarding the
piping systems on such property. The refusal of access or refusal of requested
pertinent information shall be deemed evidence of the presence of cross-
connections.
(Ord. 2018-04, passed 5-7-2018) Penalty, see §
52.99
§ 52.44 DISCONNECTION FOR CROSS-CONNECTION; RIGHT TO HEARING.
   (A)   (1)   The Town Water Utility is hereby authorized and directed to
discontinue water service to any property wherein any connection in violation
of this subchapter exists and to take such other precautionary measures deemed
necessary to eliminate any danger of contamination of the public water system.
      (2)   Water service shall be discontinued only after reasonable notice is
served on the owner, lessee or occupant of the property or premises where a
violation is found. Water service to such property shall not be restored until
the cross-connection(s) has been eliminated in compliance with the provisions
of this subchapter. A reasonable notice is deemed to be 30 days for purpose of
this section.
   (B)   If it is deemed by the town water utility that a cross-connection
endangers public health, safety or welfare and requires immediate action, and a
written finding to that effect is filed with the Clerk- Treasurer of the town
and delivered to the consumer’s premises, it may be immediately discontinued.
The consumer shall have an opportunity for hearing within ten days of such an
emergency discontinuance.
(Ord. 2018-04, passed 5-7-2018) Penalty, see §
52.99
§ 52.45 BACKFLOW PREVENTER REQUIRED FOR CERTAIN USERS.
   (A)   (1)   All consumers using toxic or hazardous liquids, all hospitals,
mortuaries, wastewater treatment plants, laboratories and all other hazardous
users shall install and maintain a reduce-pressure principle backflow preventer
in the main water line serving each building on the premises.
      (2)   The backflow preventer must be installed in an easily accessible
location not subject to flooding or freezing.
   (B)   Plants or facilities as listed need a backflow prevention device:
      (1)   Auxiliary water systems;
      (2)   Beverage bottling plants;
      (3)   Aircraft and missile plants;
      (4)   Breweries;
      (5)   Buildings, hotels, apartment houses;
      (6)   Public and private or any other structures having unprotected
cross-connections, with the exception of single-family residential structures
with existing cross-connection. All single-family residential structures that
develop cross-connection after passage of this subchapter will be subject to
this section, and said devices will be provided by the town;
      (7)   Carwash facilities;
      (8)   Chemical plants, manufacturing, processing, compounding or
treatment;
      (9)   Chemical-contaminated water systems;
      (10)   Fire systems;
      (11)   Mortuaries, autopsy facilities;
      (12)   Irrigation systems, premises having separate systems, playgrounds,
cemeteries;
      (13)   Laundries and dye works;
      (14)   Metal manufacturing, cleaning, processing and fabrication plants;
      (15)   Oil and gas production, storage or transmission properties;
      (16)   Power plants, restricted, classified or other closed facilities;
      (17)   Sand and gravel plants; and
      (18)   Sewage and storm drain facilities.
(Ord. 2018-04, passed 5-7-2018) Penalty, see §
52.99
§ 52.46 NOTICE ISSUANCE; REMEDIES PURSUED.
   (A)   The town water utility will issue a notice of violation to any person
it determines has or is violating any provisions of this subchapter. This
notice will state the nature of the violation, the action to be taken to
correct the violation, the time during which the corrective action must be
taken and the fines, penalties and remedies available to the town water utility
if the violation is not corrected.
   (B)   If the violation is not corrected as provided for in the notice, the
town water utility may exercise the following remedies, either separately or
jointly.
      (1)   Fines. The violator will be subject to a fine in the amount of $500
per day for each day, beginning when the time allowed for correction ends,
until the violation is corrected.
      (2)   Injunction. The town water utility is entitled to obtain, from a
court of competent jurisdiction, an order enjoining the violator from the
continued violation of this subchapter.
      (3)   Attorney fees. The town water utility is entitled to collect, from
the violator, any and all reasonable attorney fees it incurs in the prosecution
of any enforcement action.
      (4)   Money judgment. The town water utility is entitled to obtain, from
a court of competent jurisdiction, a money judgment equal to fines, court costs
and attorney fees as provided in this subchapter.
      (5)   Remediation. The town water utility is entitled to obtain, from a
court of competent jurisdiction, an order allowing a representative of the town
water utility to:
         (a)   Enter upon the property of the violator in order to remediate
the violation; and
         (b)   Obtain a money judgment against the violator for the expense
incurred by the utility in remediating the violation.
      (6)   Damages suffered by the utility. The town water utility is entitled
to obtain, from a court of competent jurisdiction, a money judgment for any
damages to its water supply, including, but not limited to, the cost of
decontamination, inspection, testing, provision of alternate water supply and
other damages, and for damages to its fixtures, equipment and property caused
by the violation of this section.
      (7)   Disconnection from the system. The town water utility is entitled
to disconnect the violator’s water system from the town water utility’s water
system without further notice if the violation is a danger to public health, as
provided in §
52.44(B) of this chapter.
      (8)   Other remedies. The town water utility is entitled to all other
remedies provided for by state law for a violation of this section.
(Ord. 2018-04, passed 5-7-2018) Penalty, see §
52.99
UNAUTHORIZED RECONNECTIONS
§ 52.60 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   UNAUTHORIZED INDIVIDUAL. Any person, firm or corporation who is not employed
by the town or does not have specific written permission from the town to
reconnect water service to a water service user in the town.
(Ord. 2021-03, passed 4-5-2021)
§ 52.61 UNAUTHORIZED RECONNECTION PROHIBITED.
   No unauthorized individual shall reconnect the water service to a water
service user in the town.
(Ord. 2021-03, passed 4-5-2021) Penalty, see §
52.99
§ 52.62 PRESUMPTION THAT USER RECONNECTED SERVICE.
   In the event that water service is reconnected without authorization of the
town to a water service user who has previously been disconnected by the town,
there shall be a rebuttable presumption that the resident of the dwelling or
business where the water service is provided is the unauthorized individual who
reconnected the water service.
(Ord. 2021-03, passed 4-5-2021) Penalty, see §
52.99
§ 52.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   Any person or persons violating any provisions, rules or regulations
of §§
52.20 through
52.24 of this chapter, or any amendments hereafter made thereto, wherein no
penalty is fixed shall be subject to a fine of not less than $5 and not more
than $50.
   (C)   (1)   Any person, firm or corporation who is found to be in violation
of any provisions of §§
52.60 through
52.62 of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be fined in any sum not exceeding
$500, subject to the following:
         (a)   The minimum fine for a first offense shall be the sum of $150;
         (b)   The minimum fine for a second offense shall be the sum of $300;
and
         (c)   The minimum fine for a third or subsequent offense shall be the
sum of $400.
      (2)   In addition, any person who is convicted for an offense under §§
52.60 through
52.62 of this chapter shall reimburse the town for any damage caused to the
equipment of the town by the unauthorized individual.
(Ord. 1948-2, passed 10-4-1948; Ord. 2021-03, passed 4-5-2021)

rendered by the waterworks system of the town, the following rates and charges
