PARKING
§ 71.01 PARKING ORIENTATION AND DISTANCE REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   No vehicle shall be parked on the left side of such vehicle next to
the curb except on one-way streets, and it shall be unlawful to stop or park
any vehicle in a street other than parallel with the curb and with the two
right wheels of the vehicle within 12 inches of the regularly established
curbline, except that upon those streets that have been marked for angle
parking, vehicles shall be parked at the angle to curb indicated by such marks.
   (B)   All parked vehicles on two-way streets must be parked to the right of
the roadway near the curb headed north when parked on the east side, south when
parked on the west side, east when parked on the south side and west when
parked on the north side.
(Ord. 1987-7, passed - -) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.02 SIDEWALK, PARKWAY OR CURB PARKING.
   It shall be unlawful to park on any sidewalk, parkway or curb.
(Ord. 1987-7, passed - -) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.03 NO PARKING AREAS DESIGNATED.
   No person shall park or permit to be parked any motor vehicle in a no
parking area designated by signs and yellow-painted curbing.
(Ord. 1987-7, passed - -) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.04 INOPERABLE VEHICLE PARKING.
   No person shall park or permit any inoperable motor vehicle, trailer or
camper registered in his or her name to be parked on any street or alley for a
longer consecutive period of time than 48 hours.
(Ord. 1987-7, passed - -) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.05 PROHIBITED PARKING AREAS; EXCEPTION.
   It shall be unlawful for the operator of any vehicle to stop, stand or park
the same at any time for any purpose in any of the following places, except
when necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic or in compliance with the
directions of a police officer or traffic-control sign or signal:
   (A)   Within an intersection;
   (B)   On a crosswalk;
   (C)   Between a safety zone and the adjacent curb or within 20 feet of the
points on the curb immediately opposite the ends of a safety zone unless the
Police Department shall indicate a different length by proper signs;
   (D)   Within 25 feet from the intersection of curblines;
   (E)   Within 30 feet upon the approach of any flashing beacon, stop sign or
traffic-control signal located at the side of the roadway;
   (F)   Within 15 feet of the driveway entrance to any fire station;
   (G)   Within 15 feet of any fire hydrant;
   (H)   In front of any private driveway;
   (I)   On a sidewalk;
   (J)   Alongside of or opposite any street excavation or obstruction when
such stopping, standing or parking would obstruct traffic;
   (K)   Alongside of or opposite any parked vehicle (commonly known as “double
parking”); or
   (L)   Upon any bridge or under any elevation within the town limits.
(Ord. 1987-7, passed - -) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.06 HANDICAPPED PARKING.
   (A)   Definition. For the purpose of this section, the following definition
shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different
meaning.
      PHYSICALLY HANDICAPPED PERSON or HANDICAPPED. Either having a physical
condition requiring the use of a wheelchair, artificial limb, crutch, cane or
walker, or having a physical disease making it difficult or impossible to walk
more than 25 feet without shortness of breath or danger of impairment of
health. A certificate by a person licensed to practice the healing arts in the
state shall be acceptable by the town as evidence under this section.
   (B)   Spaces designated, marked.
      (1)   For every 20 parking spaces in front of or adjacent to any public
building in the town, there shall be at least one parking space for physically
handicapped persons, which space shall be distinctly marked with either the
international wheelchair parking sign and/or clearly marked and designated
pavement of the parking stall or space displaying the international wheelchair
sign or some similar designation.
      (2)   Any further signs or designated parking spaces shall be created
upon the showing of need and upon the recommendation of the Town Council, which
shall include, but not be limited to, church parking lots, library parking lots
and other town parking spaces.
      (3)   The town shall provide for signs to be erected designating such
parking spaces, which signs shall be adjacent to and visible from such parking
stalls.
   (C)   Parking restricted. It shall be unlawful for any person to park or
leave standing any vehicle in a parking stall or parking space designated for
physically handicapped persons if, immediately adjacent to and visible from
such stall or space, there is posted a sign known as the international
wheelchair symbol, consisting of a profile view of a stylized wheelchair with
occupant in white on a blue background, or the designation of such sign is on
the pavement of the parking stall or space, unless the driver of the vehicle or
passenger of the vehicle is handicapped as defined herein.
   (D)   Signs to conform to standards. It is further ordained that the signs
to be erected shall conform to the manual on traffic-control device standards
for designating handicap parking and shall be erected in a manner that does not
create a traffic hazard.
(Ord. 1996-14, passed 12-2-1996) Penalty, see §
71.99
LOADING
§ 71.20 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   LOADING AND UNLOADING. The removal of goods from or putting goods onto a
truck, trailer, wagon, tractor or a vehicle shall be considered loading or
unloading when the driver of such vehicle is physically present or within 100
feet of said vehicle when it is running or operating.
(Ord. 1987-7, passed - -) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.21 LOADING ZONES AND PASSENGER ZONES DESIGNATED.
   The town police shall determine and designate passenger zones and loading
zones.
(Ord. 1987-7, passed - -) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.22 PASSENGER ZONE LOADING, UNLOADING TIME LIMIT.
   It shall be unlawful for the operator of a vehicle to stop, stand or park
the same for a longer period of time than is necessary for the expeditious
loading or unloading of passengers in any place designated and marked as a
passenger zone.
(Ord. 1987-7, passed - -) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   Any person violating any provision of §§
71.01 through
71.05 or
71.20 through
71.22 of this chapter shall be guilty of a Class C infraction.
   (C)   Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision of §
71.06 of this chapter shall be fined not less than $5 nor more than $100 for
each offense, and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day
during or on which the violation occurs or continues.
(Ord. 1987-7, passed - -; Ord. 1996-14, passed 12-2-1996)
CHAPTER 72: RECREATIONAL VEHICLES

GOLF CARTS
§ 72.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   DRIVER’S LICENSE. A valid license to operate a motor vehicle issued by this
state or any other state.
   FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY. Liability insurance coverage on a golf cart in an
amount not less than required by state law for motor vehicles operated on
public highways in the state.
   GOLF CART. A vehicle originally designed for operation on a golf course and
powered by a battery or internal combustion engine.
   VEHICLE. Any device or machine that transports persons, animals or property.
(Ord. 2009-05, passed 11-2-2009)
§ 72.02 GOLF CART USE REGULATED.
   The operation of a golf cart within the town is strictly prohibited unless
the golf cart is operated and equipped in full compliance with this subchapter.
(Ord. 2009-05, passed 11-2-2009) Penalty, see § 72.99
§ 72.03 OPERATOR REQUIREMENTS.
   Only persons at least 16 years of age and holding a driver’s license may
operate a golf cart on a street or alley in the town.
(Ord. 2009-05, passed 11-2-2009) Penalty, see § 72.99
§ 72.04 FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY.
   The operator of a golf cart must be in possession of proof of financial
responsibility at all times while operating a golf cart in the town.
(Ord. 2009-05, passed 11-2-2009) Penalty, see § 72.99
§ 72.05 TIME OF OPERATION.
   Golf carts shall not be operated on a town street or alley between one-half
hour before sunset and one-half hour after sunrise unless the golf cart is
equipped with two operating headlights (one on each side of the front of the
golf cart) and two operating taillights with brake lights (one on each side of
the rear of the golf cart) which are visible from a distance of 500 feet.
(Ord. 2009-05, passed 11-2-2009) Penalty, see § 72.99
§ 72.06 PLACE OF OPERATION.
   Golf carts may be operated on town streets and alleys within the town,
subject to the following: golf carts may not be operated on sidewalks or on
State Highway 32 (Main Street) or State Highway 1, except to cross said
highways at intersections in a path 90 degrees to said highways.
(Ord. 2009-05, passed 11-2-2009) Penalty, see § 72.99
§ 72.07 OCCUPANT RESTRICTIONS, REQUIREMENTS.
   The number of occupants in a golf cart shall be limited to the number of
persons for whom factory seating is installed and provided on the golf cart.
The operator and all occupants shall be seated in the golf cart at all times,
and no parts of the bodies of the operator or any occupant shall extend outside
the perimeter of the golf cart while the golf cart is being operated.
(Ord. 2009-05, passed 11-2-2009) Penalty, see § 72.99
§ 72.08 COMPLIANCE WITH MOTOR VEHICLE TRAFFIC RULES.
   The operator of the golf cart shall comply with all traffic rules and
regulations adopted by the state and by the town which govern the operation of
motor vehicles.
(Ord. 2009-05, passed 11-2-2009) Penalty, see § 72.99
§ 72.09 SLOW MOVING VEHICLE SIGN.
   All golf carts must display on the back of the golf cart a “slow moving
vehicle” sign of the same type required under state law for display on slow
moving vehicles.
(Ord. 2009-05, passed 11-2-2009) Penalty, see § 72.99
§ 72.10 LIABILITY OF PARENTS OR GUARDIANS.
   No person shall permit his or her minor child or ward to operate a golf cart
in violation of this subchapter. In the event that a minor is found to be
operating a golf cart within the town limits, there shall be a rebuttable
presumption that the minor child was operating the golf cart with the
permission and knowledge of his or her parent or guardian.
(Ord. 2009-05, passed 11-2-2009) Penalty, see § 72.99

SCHEDULE III. ONE-WAY TRAFFIC.
   (A)   One-way alleys designated.
      (1)   This division (A) shall prescribe one-way alleys within the town
for regulating the flow of traffic on the certain alleys within the town. It
shall be unlawful to operate any vehicle on any street or alley designated as a
one-way street or alley by this division (A) in any direction other than that
so designated.
         (a)   The alley on the south side of the town fire station shall be
designated for one-way traffic from Fire Street to Plum Street.
         (b)   The alley on the north side of the town fire station shall be
designated for one-way traffic (east) from Plum Street to Fire Street.
      (2)   The Town Marshal, or any person designated by the Council, shall
post or cause to be posted suitable signs for both one-way alleys.
   (B)   Additional one-way alley.
      (1)   The first alley south of Henry Street in the town shall be declared
to be a one-way alley in the easterly direction between State Road 32 and South
Plum Street, said alley being the alley which runs along the north side of Lot
137 and Lot 138 of the original plat of the town and along the south side of
Lots 129, 130, 131, 132, 133, 134, 135 and 136 of the original plat of the
town.
      (2)   No person shall operate any vehicle in a westerly direction on the
first alley south of Henry Street between State Road 32 and South Plum Street
in the town, said alley being the alley which runs along the north side of Lot
137 and Lot 138 of the original plat of the town and along the south side of
Lots 129, 130, 131, 132, 133, 134, 135 and 136 of the original plat of the
town.
   (C)   One-way parking lot. The town parking lot in the alley located on the
east side of the City Building, which is more specifically described as Lot 132
in the original plat of the town, shall now be designated as a one-way alley
traveling from south to north for the purposes of traffic flow.
   (D)   Penalty.
      (1)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
      (2)   Any person violating any of the provisions of division (A) above
shall be guilty of a Class C infraction as defined in I.C. 34-4-32-4(c) and,
upon conviction, shall be fined accordingly.
      (3)   Any person, firm, corporation or other entity violating the terms
and provisions of division (B) above shall be guilty of a Class B infraction.
      (4)   Any person, company or corporation violating any provisions of
division (C) above shall be guilty of an infraction and, upon conviction, shall
be fined in a sum of not less than $1 and not more than $100.
(Ord. -, passed 8-4-1986; Ord. 98-13, passed 11-16-1998; Ord. 2000-02, passed
7-3-2000)
SCHEDULE IV. VEHICLE SIZE RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   Restrictions. No person, persons or corporation shall operate or cause
to be operated any truck, trailer, wagon, tractor or any motor vehicle, or any
combination of the foregoing, on the following streets in the town should the
length of the vehicle, or any combination of any of the foregoing, have a
combined length of over 19 feet, or a vehicle which weighs and/or is licensed
to carry over 26,000 pounds, as evidenced by its gross vehicle weight:
      (1)   Henry Street;
      (2)   Plum Street;
      (3)   North Mulberry Street;
      (4)   North Olive Street; or
      (5)   North Hickory Street.
   (B)   Exception. It is an exception to this schedule if the person, persons
or corporation is operating a vehicle on Henry Street, Plum Street, North
Mulberry Street, North Olive Street or North Hickory Street for the sole
purpose of making a local delivery to a business located within the corporation
limits of the town.
   (C)   Penalty.
      (1)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
      (2)   Any person, persons or corporation found guilty of a violation of
division (A) above shall be subject to a fine not to exceed $500.
(Ord. 2006-07, passed 10-2-2006)

SCHEDULE I. NO PARKING.
   (A)   Rights-of-way. The following streets in the town are ordained to be
“no parking” zones, to wit:
      (1)   Each side of Fire Street;
      (2)   East side of East Street;
      (3)   East side of Gym Street from East Pursley to Church Street;
      (4)   East side of Mulberry Street between Williams Street and Henry
Street;
      (5)   East side of North Plum Street from New York Central Railroad
tracks to Jackson Street;

Street;

Mulberry Street and Hickory Street;

side of Beechwood;

and Morris Street in any direction;

Street;

Street;

each alley that intersects with North Plum Street; the curb of the sidewalk
that runs adjacent to the west side of North Plum Street shall be marked with
yellow paint to identify the areas that are within 15 feet of the center of any

      (1)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
      (2)   Any person, company or corporation violating division (A) above
shall be guilty of an infraction and, upon conviction, shall be fined a sum of
not more than $50 and not less than $10, plus court costs or the applicable
fine imposed by Winchester City Court at the time.
(Ord. 96-08, passed 9-9-1996; Ord. 2006-02, passed 4-4-2006; Ord. 2015-04,
passed 8-3-2015; Ord. 2022-04, passed 10-4-2022)
SCHEDULE II. PARALLEL OR ANGLE PARKING.
   (A)   Parallel parking. The following streets in the town are ordained to be
“parallel parking only” zones, to wit:
      (1)   North side of Williams Street between Main Street and Mulberry
Street; and
      (2)   South side of Williams Street between Mulberry Street and Hickory
Street.
   (B)   Angle parking. The following streets in the town are ordained to be
“angle parking only” zones, to wit:
      (1)   North side of Henry Street between Main Street and Mulberry Street;
      (2)   North side of Henry Street between Main Street and Plum Street, in
front or parallel to the bank;
      (3)   South side of Henry Street between Main Street and Mulberry Street;
and
      (4)   South side of Henry Street between Main Street and Plum Street.
   (C)   Penalty.
      (1)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
      (2)   Any persons, company or corporations violating division (A) or (B)
above shall be guilty of an infraction and, upon conviction, shall be fined a
sum of not more than $50 and not less than $10, plus court costs or the
applicable fine imposed by Winchester City Court at the time.
(Ord. 96-08, passed 9-9-1996)
SCHEDULE III. HANDICAPPED PARKING.
   (A)   Public parking lots. The general town parking lot(s) and the post
office parking lot shall have handicapped parking spots designated.
   (B)   108 West Henry Street. The town designates that the two parking spaces
in front of 108 West Henry Street be designated as “handicap parking spaces,”
in accordance with §
71.06 of this code. The designated parking spaces shall be clearly marked in
accordance with §
71.06. No person shall park or leave standing any vehicle in the above-
designated handicap parking spaces unless such person is handicapped as defined
by §
71.06, and who has a designated handicapped sticker or placard issued by the
appropriate issuing agency.
   (C)   Penalty.
      (1)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
      (2)   Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision of division
(A) or (B) above shall be fined not less than $5 nor more than $100 for each
offense, and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day during or
on which the violation occurs or continues.
(Ord. 1996-14, passed 12-2-1996; Ord. 97-09, passed 8-4-1997; Ord. 2011-02,
passed 3-7-2011)
SCHEDULE IV. FIFTEEN-MINUTE PARKING.
   (A)   In front of City Building.
      (1)   One parking space directly in front of the City Building, located
104 East Henry Street, Farmland, Indiana, shall be designated to be a 15-minute
parking space between the hours of 8:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m., Monday through
Friday, so as to make it more convenient for the residents of the town to have
access to the City Building.
      (2)   The town is hereby authorized to post a sign designating said
parking space with a time limit of 15 minutes and is hereby authorized to
enforce said parking time limit.
   (B)   In front of 141 East Henry Street.
      (1)   The town hereby designates that the two parking spaces in front of
141 East Henry Street, which are the first two parking spaces on the north side
of Henry Street to the west of the first alley east of Main Street, shall be
designated as a 15-minute parking zone on Saturdays from 8:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m.
      (2)   The designated parking spaces shall be clearly marked with signs
indicating that the spaces are in the 15-minute parking zone.
      (3)   No person shall park or leave standing any vehicle in the above-
designated 15-minute parking zone on Saturdays between the hours of 8:00 a.m.
and 5 p.m. for any period exceeding 15 consecutive minutes.
      (4)   There shall be a rebuttable presumption that the registered owner
of the vehicle parked and standing in the 15-minute parking zone is the
individual that caused the vehicle to be parked in the zone.
   (C)   Penalty.
      (1)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
      (2)   Any person, company or corporation violating any provisions of
division (A) above shall be guilty of an infraction and, upon conviction, shall
be fined in a sum of not less than $1 and not more than $100.
      (3)   (a)   A person found guilty of violating division (B) above shall
be fined not less than $25 and not more than $100 for each offense. A separate
offense shall be deemed committed for each additional 15-minute period for
which the person parks and leaves the vehicle in such zone.
         (b)   Any vehicle which is parked in the 15-minute parking zone set
out in division (B) above for a period exceeding one consecutive hour may be
towed at the expense of the owner of the vehicle. The owner of such vehicle
shall be notified of the location of the vehicle, in writing, within three
business days of the date the vehicle is towed. The owner of the vehicle which
is towed shall be responsible to pay the towing and/or storage fee directly to
the towing company.
(Ord. 98-12, passed 11-2-1998; Ord. 2013-02, passed 2-4-2013)
SCHEDULE V. SNOW EMERGENCY RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   Public policy declared. It is declared to be in the best interest of
the public policy and the public safety of the town to regulate and restrict
the parking of vehicles on public streets during snow emergencies.
   (B)   Snow emergency defined. For the purpose of this schedule, the
following definition shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or
requires a different meaning.
      SNOW EMERGENCY. A period of time after a forecast by the United States
Weather Bureau during and after a snowfall during which vehicular traffic is
expected to be particularly hazardous or congested due to the elements, and
during which period of time the parking of vehicles could hinder, delay and
obstruct the safe flow of traffic and the proper cleaning, clearing and making
safe of certain heavily traveled public streets of this town.
   (C)   Snow control routes designated. Which streets shall be designated snow
control routes are as follows, to wit:
      (1)   New York Street;
      (2)   East and West Williams Street;
      (3)   North and South Mulberry Street;
      (4)   North and South Plum Street; and
      (5)   East and West Henry Street.
   (D)   Town Council to declare snow emergency.
      (1)   A snow emergency shall commence by executive order, determination
and or proclamation by the Town Council or other designated town official, such
as the Town Marshal, or if declared by the county, as issued to local radio,
television and news services either before, during or after a snowfall, when in
the Council’s sound judgment and discretion, the circumstances warrant the
determination of such an emergency for the public safety of the town.
      (2)   The snow emergency shall continue in effect until the Council
determines that an emergency no longer exists and accordingly terminates the
emergency using the same media as before.
   (E)   Penalty. It is hereby declared that any vehicle not moved during such
a designated snow emergency shall be towed to the town-owned property or to a
private garage, where the vehicle may be impounded and shall be released only
at the owner’s expense.
(Ord. 96-07, passed 9-9-1996)
SCHEDULE VI. VEHICLE SIZE RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   General prohibition; Main Street exception. No person, persons or
corporation shall park or cause to be parked any truck, trailer, wagon, tractor
or any motor vehicle, or any combination of any of the foregoing, on the town
streets or alleys of the town, except Main Street, should their length or any
combination of the foregoing have a combined length of over 19 feet, except
when loading or unloading.
   (B)   Prohibitions on certain streets.
      (1)   No person, persons or corporation shall park, or cause to be
parked, any truck, trailer, wagon, tractor or any motor vehicle, or any
combination of the foregoing, on any of the streets in the town should the
length of the vehicle, or any combination of any of the foregoing, have a
combined length of over 19 feet, or a vehicle which weighs and/or is licensed
to carry over 26,000 pounds as evidenced by its gross vehicle weight.
      (2)   It is an exception to this division (B) if the person, persons or
corporation is operating a vehicle for the sole purpose of making a local
delivery to a business located within the corporation limits of the town.
      (3)   There is a rebuttable presumption that the registered owner of a
vehicle caused the vehicle to be parked in the location at which the vehicle is
found if the vehicle is found to be parked on and street within the town
limits.
   (C)   Penalty.
      (1)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
      (2)   Any person violating any provisions of division (A) above shall be
guilty of a Class C infraction.
      (3)   Any person, persons or corporation found guilty of a violation of
division (B) above shall be subject to a fine not to exceed $500.
(Ord. 1987-7, passed - -; Ord. 2006-07, passed 10-2-2006)

CHAPTER 90: FAIR HOUSING
Section
   
90.01   Policy statement
   
90.02   Definitions
   
90.03   Unlawful practice
   
90.04   Discrimination in the sale, rental of housing
   
90.05   Discrimination in residential real estate-related transactions
   
90.06   Discrimination in the provision of brokerage service
   
90.07   Interference, coercion or intimidation
   
90.08   Prevention of intimidation in fair housing cases
   
90.09   Equal access to housing in HUD programs
   
90.10   Exemptions
   
90.11   Administrative enforcement
 
   
90.99   Penalty
§ 90.01 POLICY STATEMENT.
   It shall be the policy of the town to provide, within constitutional
limitation, for fair housing throughout its corporate limits as provided for
under the federal Civil Rights Act of 1968, as amended, the federal Housing and
Community Development Act of 1974, as amended, and I.C. 22-9.5-1 et seq.
(Ord. 2013-06, passed 5-17-2013)
§ 90.02 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   AGGRIEVED PERSON. Any person who (I.C. 22-9.5-2-2):
      (1)   Claims to have been injured by a discriminatory housing practice;
or
      (2)   Believes that such person will be injured by a discriminatory
housing practice that is about to occur.
   COMMISSION. The state’s Civil Rights Commission, created pursuant to I.C.
22-9-1-4 et seq.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-3)
   COMPLAINANT. A person, including the Commission, who files a complaint under
I.C. 22-9.5-6.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-4)
   DISCRIMINATORY HOUSING PRACTICE. An act that is unlawful under §§
90.04 through
90.08 of this chapter or I.C. 22-9.5-5.
   DWELLING. Any building, structure or part of a building or structure that is
occupied as, or designed or intended for occupancy as, a residence by one or
more families; or any vacant land which is offered for sale or lease for the
construction or location of a building, structure or part of a building or
structure that is occupied as, or designed or intended for occupancy as, a
residence by one or more families.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-8)
   FAMILIAL STATUS. One or more individuals who have not attained the age of 18
years being domiciled with a parent or another person having legal custody of
such individual or the written permission of such parent or other person. The
protections afforded against discrimination on the basis of FAMILIAL STATUS
shall apply to any person who is pregnant or is in the process of securing
legal custody of any individual who has not attained the age of 18 years.
   FAMILY. Includes a single individual (I.C. 22-9.5-2-9), with the status of
such FAMILY being further defined in the definition of “familial status” in
this section.
   HANDICAP.
      (1)   With respect to a person:
         (a)   A physical or mental impairment which substantially limits one
or more of such person’s major life activities;
         (b)   A record of having such an impairment;
         (c)   Being regarded as having such an impairment;
         (d)   An impairment described or defined pursuant to the federal
Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990; or
         (e)   Any other impairment defined under I.C. 22-9.5-2-10.
      (2)   The term HANDICAP shall not include current illegal use of or
addictions to a controlled substance as defined in 21 U.S.C. § 802 (I.C. 22-
9.5-2-10(b)), nor does the term HANDICAP include an individual solely because
that individual is a transvestite (I.C. 22-9.5-2-10(c)).
   PERSON. Includes one or more individuals, corporations, partnerships,
associations, labor organizations, legal representatives, mutual companies,
joint stock companies, trusts, non-incorporated organizations, trustees,
trustees in cases under 11 U.S.C., receivers and fiduciaries.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-11)
   TO RENT. Includes to lease, to sublease, to let and otherwise to grant for a
consideration the rights to occupy the premises owned by the occupant.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-13)
(Ord. 2013-06, passed 5-17-2013)
§ 90.03 UNLAWFUL PRACTICE.
   Subject to the provisions of division (B) below, §
90.09 of this chapter and I.C. 22-9.5-3, the prohibitions against
discrimination in the sale or rental of housing set forth in I.C. 22-9.5-5-
1 and in §
90.04 of this chapter shall apply to:
   (A)   All dwellings, except as exempted by division (B) below and I.C. 22-
9.5-3;
   (B)   Other than the provisions of division (C) below, nothing in §
90.04 of this chapter shall apply to:
      (1)   Any single-family house sold or rented by an owner where the
private individual owner does not own more than three such single-family houses
at any one time; provided that in the sale of such single-family house by a
private individual owner not residing in the house at the time of sale or
exemption, shall apply only to one such sale within any 24-month period. The
private individual owner may not own any interest in, nor have owned or
reserved on his or her behalf, title to or any right to all or a portion of the
proceeds from the sale or rental of more than three such single-family houses
at any one time. The sale or rental of any such single-family house shall be
exempted from application of this section only if such house is sold or rented:
         (a)   Without the use in any manner of the sales or rental facilities
or services of any real estate broker, agent or salesperson, or any person in
the business of selling or renting dwellings, or of any employee or agent of
any such broker, agent or salesperson, or person; and
         (b)   Without the publication, posting or mailing, after notice of
advertisement or written notice in violation of §
90.04(C) of this chapter, but noting in this provision shall prohibit the use
of attorneys, escrow agents, abstracters, title companies and other such
professional assistance as necessary to perfect or transfer the title.
      (2)   Rooms or units in dwellings containing living quarters occupied or
intended to be occupied by not more than four families living independently of
each other, if the owner actually maintains and occupies one of such living
quarters as his or her residence.
   (C)   For the purposes of division (B) above, a person shall be deemed to be
in the business of selling or renting dwellings if:
      (1)   They have, within the preceding 12 months, participated as
principal in three or more transactions involving the sale or rental of any
dwelling or any interest therein;
      (2)   They have, within the preceding 12 months, participated as agent,
other than in the sale of his or her own personal residence, in providing sales
or rental facilities or services in two or more transactions involving the sale
or rental of any dwelling or any interest therein; or
      (3)   They are the owner of any dwelling unit designed or intended for
occupancy by, or occupied by, five or more families.
(Ord. 2013-06, passed 5-17-2013)
§ 90.04 DISCRIMINATION IN THE SALE, RENTAL OF HOUSING.
   As made applicable by §
90.03 of this chapter, and except as exempted by §§
90.03(B) and
90.09 of this chapter, it shall be unlawful:
   (A)   To refuse to sell or rent after the making of a bona fide offer, or to
refuse to negotiate for the sale or rental of, or otherwise make unavailable or
deny, a dwelling to any person because of race, color, religion, sex, handicap,
familial status or national origin;
   (B)   To discriminate against any person in the terms, conditions or
privileges of sale or rental of a dwelling, or in the provision of services of
facilities in connection therewith, because of race, color, religion, sex,
handicap, familial status or national origin;
   (C)   To make, print or publish, or to cause to be made, printed or
published, any notice, statement or advertisement, with respect to the sale or
rental of a dwelling, that indicates any preference, limitation or
discrimination based on race, color, religion, sex, handicap, familial status
or national origin, or an intention to make any such preference, limitation or
discrimination;
   (D)   To represent to any person because of race, color, religion, sex,
handicap, familial status or national origin that any dwelling is not available
for inspection, sale or rental when such dwelling is in fact so available;
   (E)   For profit, to induce or attempt to induce any person to sell or rent
any dwelling by representations regarding the entry or perspective entry into
the neighborhood of a person or persons of a particular race, color, religion,
sex, handicap, familial status or national origin;
   (F)   To discriminate in the sale or rental, or to otherwise make
unavailable or deny, a dwelling to any buyer or renter because of a handicap
of:
      (1)   That buyer or renter;
      (2)   A person residing in, or intending to reside in, that dwelling
after it is so sold, rented or made available; or
      (3)   Any person associated with that person.
   (G)   To discriminate against any person in the terms, conditions or
privileges of sale or rental of a dwelling, or in the provision of services or
facilities in connection with such dwelling, because of a handicap of:
      (1)   That person;
      (2)   A person residing in, or intending to reside in, that dwelling
after it is so sold, rented or made available; or
      (3)   Any person associated with that person.
   (H)   (1)   For purposes of this division (H), discrimination includes:
         (a)   A refusal to permit, at the expense of the handicapped person,
reasonable modifications of existing premises occupied or to be occupied by
such person if such modifications may be necessary to afford such person full
enjoyment of the premises, except that, in the case of a rental, the landlord
or landlady may, where it is reasonable to do so, condition permission for a
modification on the renter agreeing to restore the interior of the premises to
the condition that existed before the modifications, reasonable wear and tear
excepted;
         (b)   A refusal to make reasonable accommodations in rules, policies,
practices or services when such accommodations may be necessary to afford such
person equal opportunity to use and enjoy a dwelling; or
         (c)   In connection with the design and construction of covered multi-
family dwellings for first occupancy after the date that is 30 months after
September 13, 1998, a failure to design and construct those dwellings in such a
manner that:
            1.   The public use and common use portions of such dwellings are
readily accessible to and usable by handicapped persons;
            2.   All the doors designed to allow passage into and within all
premises within such dwellings are sufficiently wide to allow passage by
handicapped persons in wheelchairs; and
            3.   All premises within such dwellings contain the following
features of adaptive design:
               a.   An accessible route into and through the dwelling;
               b.   Light, switches, electrical outlets, thermostats and other
environmental controls in accessible locations;
               c.   Reinforcements in bathrooms such that an individual in a
wheelchair can maneuver about the space.
      (2)   Compliance with the appropriate requirements of the Americans with
Disabilities Act of 1990 and the American National Standard for Buildings and
Facilities providing accessibility and usability for physically handicapped
people (commonly cited as ANSI A117.1) suffices to satisfy the requirements of
division (H)(1)(c)3.c. above.
      (3)   Nothing in this division (H) requires that a dwelling be made
available to an individual whose tenancy would constitute a direct threat to
the health or safety of other individuals or whose tenancy would result in
substantial physical damage to the property of others.
(Ord. 2013-06, passed 5-17-2013) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.05 DISCRIMINATION IN RESIDENTIAL REAL ESTATE-RELATED TRANSACTIONS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person or other entity whose business
includes engaging in residential real estate-related transactions to
discriminate against any person in making available such a transaction, or in
the terms or conditions of such a transaction, because of race, color,
religion, sex, handicap, familial status or national origin.
   (B)   As used in this section, the term RESIDENTIAL REAL ESTATE-RELATED
TRANSACTION means any of the following:
      (1)   The making or purchasing of loans or providing other financial
assistance:
         (a)   For purchasing, constructing, improving, repairing or
maintaining a dwelling; or
         (b)   Secured by residential real estate.
      (2)   The selling, brokering or appraising of residential real property.
   (C)   Nothing in this chapter prohibits a person engaged in the business of
furnishing appraisals of real property to take into consideration factors other
than race, color, religion, national origin, sex, handicap or familial status.
(Ord. 2013-06, passed 5-17-2013) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.06 DISCRIMINATION IN THE PROVISION OF BROKERAGE SERVICE.
   It shall be unlawful to deny any person access to or membership or
participation in any multiple- listing service, real estate brokers’
organization or other service, organization or facility relating to the
business of selling or renting dwellings, or to discriminate against him or her
in the terms or conditions of such access, membership or participation, on
account of race, color, religion, sex, handicap, familial status or national
origin.
(Ord. 2013-06, passed 5-17-2013) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.07 INTERFERENCE, COERCION OR INTIMIDATION.
   It shall be unlawful to coerce, intimidate, threaten or interfere with any
person in the exercise or enjoyment of, or on account of his or her having
exercised or enjoyed, or on account of his or her having aided or encouraged
any other person in the exercise or enjoyment of, any right granted or
protected by §§
90.03 through
90.06 of this chapter.
(Ord. 2013-06, passed 5-17-2013) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.08 PREVENTION OF INTIMIDATION IN FAIR HOUSING CASES.
   Whoever, whether or not acting under code or law, by force or threat of
force willfully injures, intimidates or interferes with, or attempt to injure,
intimidate or interfere with the following shall be fined and/or imprisoned
according to local, state and federal law:
   (A)   Any person because of his or her race, color, religion, sex, handicap,
familial status or national origin, and because he or she is or has been
selling, purchasing, renting, financing, occupying or contracting or
negotiating for the sale, purchase, rental, financing or occupation of any
dwelling, or applying for or participating in any service, organization or
facility relating to the business of selling or renting dwellings;
   (B)   Any person because he or she is or has been, or in order to intimidate
such person or any other person or any class of persons from:
      (1)   Participating, without discrimination on account of race, color,
religion, sex, handicap, familial status or national origin, in any of the
activities, services, organizations or facilities described in division (A)
above; or
      (2)   Affording another person or class of persons opportunity or
protection so to participate.
   (C)   Any citizen because he or she is or has been, or in order to
discourage such citizen or any other citizen from lawfully aiding or
encouraging other persons to participate, without discrimination on account of
race, color, religion, sex, handicap, familial status or national origin, in
any of the activities, services, organizations or facilities described in
division (A) above, or participating lawfully in speech or peaceful assembly
opposing any denial of the opportunity to participate.
(Ord. 2013-06, passed 5-17-2013) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.09 EQUAL ACCESS TO HOUSING IN HUD PROGRAMS.
   Pursuant to Federal Register, Volume 77, Number 23, published on February 3,
2012, the definition of FAMILY is revised to include families regardless of the
actual or perceived sexual orientation, gender identity or marital status of
its members.
(Ord. 2013-06, passed 5-17-2013)
§ 90.10 EXEMPTIONS.
   (A)   Exemptions defined or set forth under I.C. 22-9.5-3 et seq. shall be
exempt from the provisions of this chapter, to include those activities or
organizations set forth under divisions (B) and (C) below.
   (B)   Nothing in this chapter shall prohibit a religious organization,
association or society, or any nonprofit institution or organization operated,
supervised or controlled by or in conjunction with a religious organization,
association or society, from limiting the sale, rental or occupancy of
dwellings which it owns or operates for other than a commercial purpose to
persons of the same religion, or from giving preference to such persons, unless
membership in such religion is restricted on account of race, color or national
origin. Nor shall anything in this chapter prohibit a private club not in fact
open to the public which, as an incident to its primary purpose or purposes,
provides lodgings which it owns or operates for other than a commercial purpose
from limiting the rental or occupancy of such lodgings to its members or from
giving preference to its members.
   (C)   Nothing in this chapter regarding familial status shall apply with
respect to housing for older persons. As used in this section, HOUSING FOR
OLDER PERSONS means housing:
      (1)   Provided under any state or federal program that the Secretary of
the federal Department of Housing and Urban Development or the state Civil
Rights Commission determines is specifically designed and operated to assist
elderly persons (as defined in the state or federal program);
      (2)   Intended for, and solely occupied by, persons 62 years of age or
older; or
      (3)   Intended and operated for occupancy by at least one person 55 years
of age or older per unit.
(Ord. 2013-06, passed 5-17-2013)
§ 90.11 ADMINISTRATIVE ENFORCEMENT.
   (A)   The authority and responsibility for properly administering this
chapter and referral of complaints hereunder to the Commissioner, as set forth
in division (B) below, shall be vested in the chief elected official of the
town.
   (B)   Notwithstanding the provisions of I.C. 22-9.5-4-8, the town, because
of lack of financial and other resources necessary to fully administer
enforcement proceedings and possible civil actions under the chapter, herein
elects to refer all formal complaints of violation of the articles of this
chapter by complainants to the state’s Civil Rights Commission for
administrative enforcement actions pursuant to I.C. 22-9.5-6, and the chief
elected official of the town shall refer all said complaints to the Commission
as provided for under division (A) above for purposes of investigation,
resolution and appropriate relief as provided for under I.C. 22-9.5-6.
   (C)   All executive departments and agencies of the town shall administer
their departments, programs and activities relating to housing and urban
development in a manner affirmatively to further the purposes of this chapter
and shall cooperate with the chief elected official and the Commission to
further such purposes.
   (D)   The chief elected official of the town or the chief elected official’s
designee shall provide information on remedies available to any aggrieved
person or complainant requesting such information.
(Ord. 2013-06, passed 5-17-2013)
§ 90.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   If bodily injury results from a violation as set out in §
90.08 of this code, a person shall be fined not more than $10,000 or imprisoned
not more than ten years, or both, and if death results, a person shall be
subject to imprisonment for any term of years or for life.
(Ord. 2013-06, passed 5-17-2013)

GENERAL PROVISIONS AND ENFORCEMENT
§ 91.001 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ANIMAL. Any vertebrae creature imported, exotic or domesticated.
   DOMESTICATED LIVESTOCK. Any animal raised for profit.
   NUISANCE. When the owner of an animal allows said animal to violate any of
the following:
      (1)   Running at large, not being under the owner’s control, not being
confined to a cage, leash, tether, fence or the like, or by any other means of
restraint to prevent said animal from leaving the owner’s property;
      (2)   Molests or disturbs persons, vehicles or property by running,
walking, chasing, digging, barking or biting;
      (3)   Consistently barks, whines, howls, meows, cries, squawks or makes
any other noise excessively without having valid cause, thus disturbing the
peace in the area that the animal is located;
      (4)   Defecates upon any public place or private property not owned or
controlled by the animal’s owner himself or herself; note that if the owner of
said animal immediately removes the waste, he or she shall not be held in
violation;
      (5)   Creates noxious or offensive odors; or
      (6)   Creates an insect breeding or gathering site due to unsanitary
conditions.
   OWNER. Any person having purchased an animal, or having been given custody
of an animal by another, thus harboring, having care of or having charge of,
control of or possession of said animal.
   PET. Any animal bought by, or given custody to, an individual for purposes
of enjoyment, companionship, safety and other noncommercial purposes.
   RUNNING AT LARGE. Any animal not confined within its owner’s property to
prevent means of escape.
   VETERINARIAN. A person licensed to practice veterinary medicine in the
state.
   VICIOUS. Any animal which has:
      (1)   Attacked a person or another animal without having been provoked by
that person or animal;
      (2)   Attacked at some place other than its owner’s property; or
      (3)   Chased or approached another living thing at other than its owner’s
property in a menacing, threatening fashion or apparent attitude to attack.
   WILD ANIMAL. Any animal not considered a pet residing inside the town
limits.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
§ 91.002 ENFORCEMENT POWERS.
   (A)   A person individually charged with the enforcement of this chapter
shall be designated the Animal Control Officer.
      (1)   Such Officer shall have full power to enforce all provisions of
this chapter, including the right to proceed upon public and private property
within the town limits in pursuit of animals in violation of this chapter.
      (2)   Such Officer shall not have the right to enter a privately owned
enclosure in pursuit of any animal without consent of the owner, lessee or
occupant unless immediate danger warrants such to prevent injury or other legal
process is used; provided, however, if any animal is believed to be enclosed
without adequate food and water or dead animals are believed to be present with
just cause, the Animal Control Officer may attach a notice upon said structure
in an obvious location directing the occupant to contact the Officer at a given
location or phone number. If contact is not made within 24 hours, the Officer
may enter said enclosure to determine if this chapter has been violated.
   (B)   Any animal deemed vicious by the Animal Control Officer and that
cannot be captured safely without injury may be immediately destroyed for the
safety of the people of the town and its employees.
   (C)   Any animal trapped or captured in violation under this chapter shall
be held for three days at the town’s animal holding cages, with only the
following exceptions:
      (1)   Any animal that is hurt, injured, ill, sick or diseased in any way;
      (2)   Any animal too small or too large to be held in the town’s holding
cages; or
      (3)   Any animal deemed vicious or dangerous to control.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
§ 91.003 INTERFERENCE WITH ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for a person to interfere with an animal control
officer in the performance of his or her duties.
   (B)   Anyone, owner or otherwise, releasing any animal from a live trap,
cage or holding area shall be held in violation of this chapter.
   (C)   At no time shall anyone release any animal from the town’s custody
without prior knowledge of the Town Marshal or Animal Control Officer.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.004 ABSENCE OF ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER.
   At any time the Animal Control Officer is not present, the Town Marshal, or
his or her Deputies and Reserve Deputies, may enforce this chapter.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
CARE AND TREATMENT OF ANIMALS
§ 91.015 GENERAL REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   All owners of animals shall see that their animal is:
      (1)   Kept in a clean, healthy and sanitary manner so that the animal is
not to be forced to sit or lay in its own excrement;
      (2)   Adequately fed, watered and sheltered, where:
         (a)   A shelter shall have adequate ventilation from excessive heat
and protection from cold; and
         (b)   Each living area for an animal shall be of adequate size to
provide room for sufficient exercise for said animal(s).
      (3)   On a tethered leash, shall have at least 15 feet in length for
movement, and the weight of said leash shall be strong enough to confine said
animal yet allow free movement;
      (4)   Protected against abuse or mistreatment and separated from other
animals that might cause harm to each other;
      (5)   Properly cared for by a certified veterinarian should it become
sick, diseased or injured;
      (6)   Separated from other animals should it become diseased, sick, ill
or vicious; and
      (7)   Maintained in compliance with all applicable federal, state and
local laws and regulations respecting animal care or control as provided by the
Department of Public Safety.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to beat, starve or otherwise
mistreat any animal. Failure to comply with any requirement of division (A)
above shall be deemed mistreatment of the animal.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.016 ABANDONING ANIMALS.
   It is unlawful for any person(s) to abandon any animal on any property,
public or private.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.017 POISONING ANIMALS.
   It shall be unlawful to throw or deposit poisoned meat or any poison or
harmful substance on any property, public or private, with the only exception
being for rodent control.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.018 PROVOKING ANIMAL FIGHTS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to cause or incite any animals to fight
for any reason other than the personal protection of said owner.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
Penalty, see §
91.999
ANIMAL LICENSES
§ 91.030 DOG LICENSE REQUIREMENT.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to own within the town any dog six
months of age or older unless a current animal license issued by the county has
been obtained for the dog by said owner.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.031 PET SHOP LICENSE REQUIREMENT.
   A pet shop license pursuant to this section shall be displayed prominently
in the business office at all times.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
Penalty, see §
91.999
RABIES CONTROL
§ 91.045 VACCINATION REQUIRED.
   Each dog, cat or required animal shall have a rabies vaccination more recent
than one year.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.046 QUARANTINING AUTHORITY.
   For the purposes of this subchapter, the Quarantine Authority shall be the
Department of Public Safety, and any of its agents or employees so designated,
acting pursuant to the directives and regulations of the Health and Hospital
Corporation of the county.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
§ 91.047 SURRENDER OF ANIMALS.
   The owner of any person suspected by the Animal Control Officer to have
bitten any person or been exposed to rabies shall promptly surrender said
animal for purposes of quarantine and observation. This shall be at the expense
of the owner at $10 per day.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.048 RABIES AND QUARANTINE.
   (A)   Any animal found to be rabid must be held and quarantined immediately
for two weeks of observation.
   (B)   The animal owner is responsible for reimbursing the town $10 per day
and any other veterinarian expenses incurred while under the observation
period.
   (C)   Should the Town Marshal or Animal Control Officer deem an animal to be
vicious and a threat to the people of the town at the end of the two-week
period, the animal owner shall be responsible for euthanizing the animal.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
Penalty, see §
91.999
IMPOUNDMENT
§ 91.060 GROUNDS FOR IMPOUNDMENT.
   (A)   Animals found at large in violation of this chapter shall be captured
and impounded.
   (B)   Any animal found abandoned or confined on private property in
violation of this chapter shall be impounded.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.061 NOTICE TO OWNER.
   (A)   Upon the impoundment of any animal, a reasonable attempt shall be made
to notify and inform the owner of the animal of the requirements of this
subchapter for regaining custody of the animal.
   (B)   In cases of animal neglect and abuse, the Animal Control Officer may
refuse to release said animal to the original owner.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
§ 91.062 RELEASE OF CAPTURED ANIMAL WITHOUT IMPOUNDMENT.
   When the owner of a captured animal is known, such animal need not be
impounded (at the Animal Control Officer’s discretion) but may be released to
the owner upon payment of fees and fines, if any, or upon the application for
license, if required.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
§ 91.063 IMPOUNDMENT FEE.
   (A)   First offense: $10;
   (B)   Second offense: $25;
   (C)   Third offense: $50;
   (D)   Each subsequent offense: $50 additionally; and
   (E)   Each day of impoundment: $10 additionally.
(Ord. 1929-1, passed 9-9-; Ord. 1972-08, passed 10-16-1972; Ord. 1991-04,
passed 5-6-1991; Ord. 97-01, passed 5-5-1997; Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999)
BEEKEEPING
§ 91.075 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   APIARY. A location where bees are kept, also known as a BEE YARD.
   BEEKEEPING. The maintenance of honeybee colonies, commonly in human-made
hives, by humans. A beekeeper (or apiarist) keeps bees in order to collect
their honey and other products that the hive produces (including beeswax,
propolis, pollen and royal jelly), to pollinate crops or to produce bees for
sale to other beekeepers.
   PERSON. Any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or
organization of any kind.
   PROPERTY. Any real property within the town which is not a street or a
highway.
(Ord. 2017-04, passed 12-4-2017)
§ 91.076 BEEKEEPING PROHIBITED.
   No person shall maintain an apiary or practice beekeeping within the town.
(Ord. 2017-04, passed 12-4-2017) Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.077 KEEPING APIARY ON PRIVATE PROPERTY PROHIBITED.
   (A)   No person in charge or in control of any real property within the
town, whether as an owner, tenant, occupant, lessee or otherwise, shall allow
any person to maintain an apiary, or bee yard, on the property within his or
her control.
   (B)   No person in charge or in control of any real property within the
town, whether as an owner, tenant, occupant, lessee or otherwise, shall allow
any person to practice beekeeping on the property within his or her control.
(Ord. 2017-04, passed 12-4-2017) Penalty, see §
91.999
LIVESTOCK
§ 91.090 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   LIVESTOCK. A horse, cow, mule, colt, donkey, bull, ox, calf, goat, sheep,
pig, goose, chicken, turkey, duck, llama or any other animal commonly used on a
farm for the production of goods for sale.
   PERSON. Any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or
organization of any kind.
   PROPERTY. Any real property within the town which is not a street or a
highway.
(Ord. 1973-3, passed 3-5-1973; Ord. 2018-06, passed 9-4-2018)
§ 91.091 LIVESTOCK PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to keep livestock, or permit livestock
to be kept, on his or her premises in the town, whether gratuitously or for a
fee.
(Ord. 1973-3, passed 3-5-1973; Ord. 2018-06, passed 9-4-2018) Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.092 KEEPING LIVESTOCK ON PRIVATE PROPERTY PROHIBITED.
   No person in charge or in control of any real property within the town,
whether as an owner, tenant, occupant, lessee or otherwise, shall allow any
person to maintain a structure or other facility in which livestock or other
farm animals are housed or kept on any property within his or her control.
(Ord. 1973-3, passed 3-5-1973; Ord. 2018-06, passed 9-4-2018) Penalty, see §
91.999
DOG KENNELS
§ 91.105 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   DOG KENNEL.
      (1)   Any residence, building or other facility which is used primarily
to breed and raise dogs for sale;
      (2)   Any residence, building or other facility which houses more than
six dogs of any age at any one point in time; or
      (3)   Any residence, building or other facility which houses more than
two dogs which are owned for the purpose of the reproduction of offspring.
(Ord. 2000-07, passed 11-6-2000)
§ 91.106 KENNELS PROHIBITED.
   It shall be considered a violation of this section for any person, firm,
corporation or organization to house, operate or facilitate the operation of a
dog kennel within the town.
(Ord. 2000-07, passed 11-6-2000) Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.999 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   Any violation of §
91.003 of this chapter shall be punishable by a fine of not less than $50.
   (C)   (1)   Any person who violated any of the provisions of §
91.015 of this chapter may be given written notice of the practices or
conditions which constitute the violation, and the enforcing authority may,
where appropriate, suggest remedies. Any violation of this section shall be
punishable by a fine of not less than $50.
      (2)   Any person convicted of a second offense or subsequent offense of
violating provisions of §
91.015 of this chapter shall be fined in an amount of not less than $50, and
the court, upon request, shall order a forfeiture or other disposition of the
animal involved. Any judgment which calls for a fine or forfeiture or other
disposition of the animal by the town or any third party shall include the
collection costs, court costs, housing and the like as part of the judgment.
   (D)   A violation of §
91.016 of this chapter shall be punishable by a fine of not less than $50.
   (E)   The owner of an animal which does not have a rabies vaccination more
recent than one year as set out in §
91.045 of this chapter shall be punishable by a fine of the following amounts,
plus the expense to the Quarantine Authority of proving for the animal a
current rabies vaccination:
      (1)   First offense: $25;
      (2)   Second offense: $50; and
      (3)   Each consecutive offense thereafter: $50 times the number of
offenses, including the first two offenses.
   (F)   Any owner of an animal suspected to be rabid that refuses to release
said animal for observation as set out in §
91.048 of this chapter shall be fined not less than $100 per day.
   (G)   In addition to any penalty imposed under this chapter, the court shall
impose a restitution fee of $50 against any individual found in violation of
any section of this chapter if the violation results in the Animal Control
Officer utilizing any medicine, tranquilizer or any other substance in order to
effect the capture of an at-large animal as set out in §
91.060 of this chapter.
   (H)   Any person, firm or corporation who is found to be in violation of any
provisions of §§
91.075 through
91.077 of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be fined in any sum not
exceeding $500. Each day that the person is found to be in violation of §§
91.075 through
91.077 shall constitute a separate offense.
   (I)   Any person, firm or corporation who is found to be in violation of any
provisions of §§
91.090 through
91.092 of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be fined in any sum not
exceeding $500. Each day that the person is found to be in violation of §§
91.090 through
91.092 shall constitute a separate offense.
   (J)   Any person, firm, corporation or organization who is convicted of a
violation of §
91.106 of this chapter shall be subject to a fine in the following amount:
      (1)   First offense: $250 to $500, plus court costs; and
      (2)   Second offense and all subsequent offenses: $500 to $1,000, plus
court costs.
(Ord. 99-02, passed 6-7-1999; Ord. 2000-07, passed 11-6-2000; Ord. 2002-04,
passed 5-6-2002; Ord. 2017-04, passed 12-4-2017; Ord. 2018-06, passed 9-4-2018)
CHAPTER 92: HEALTH AND SANITATION; NUISANCES
Section
Housing and Sanitation Nuisances
   
92.01   Definition
   
92.02   Nuisances on premises prohibited
   
92.03   Declaring property a health hazard
   
92.04   Order to abate; time limit

Public Health Nuisances
   
92.20   Authoring or maintaining a nuisance unlawful
   92.21   Noxious substances, rank weeds and animal slaughter
   92.22   Trash disposal and weed maintenance; abatement by town
   92.23   Sanitary surveys; notice to abate; lien upon failure to abate
   92.24   Town Marshal to aid enforcement
 
   
92.99   Penalty
HOUSING AND SANITATION NUISANCES
§ 92.01 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   NUISANCE.
      (1)   Any condition of building exteriors or premises which is
detrimental to the property of others or which causes or tends to cause
substantial diminution in the value of other property in the neighborhood in
which the premises is located or the maintenance of an unsafe dwelling or
building within the town.
      (2)   In addition thereto, the term NUISANCE shall also include:
         (a)   The accumulation of, outside of dwellings or other buildings on
residential property, junk, trash or debris, including, but not limited to,
garbage, discarded and refuse materials, waste materials, leaves, iron, tin,
furniture, appliances, cans and paper; and
         (b)   The storage of any motor vehicle parts, tires or building
materials other than in an enclosed building or within an area adequately
concealed so as not to be visible from any surrounding residential or public
properties.
(Ord. 93-08, passed 2-7-1993)
§ 92.02 NUISANCES ON PREMISES PROHIBITED.
   No person owning, leasing, occupying or having charge of any premises shall
maintain or keep any nuisance thereon, nor shall any such person keep or
maintain such premises in a manner causing substantial diminution in the value
of the other property in the neighborhood in which such premises is located.
(Ord. 93-08, passed 2-7-1993) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.03 DECLARING PROPERTY A HEALTH HAZARD.
   When the property in question is in such a condition or contains sufficient
trash and debris thereon that it represents a hazard to public health, the
property may be declared a “health hazard” upon the request of a town employee
and upon the approval of the Town Marshal and will be subject to §
92.04 of this chapter.
(Ord. 97-03, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 92.04 ORDER TO ABATE; TIME LIMIT.
   (A)   Upon the showing that the property in question constitutes a “health
hazard” as described in §
92.03 of this chapter, the person violating the provisions of this subchapter
may be ordered to remedy and cure said conditions which constitute the nuisance
within one week of notification by a town employee. Such order shall be made by
the President of the Town Council or the Town Marshal or his or her designee.
   (B)   The order shall contain:
      (1)   The name of the owner or other person to whom the order is
directed;
      (2)   The legal description or address of the premises that is the
subject of the order;
      (3)   The description of the nuisance and the action the order requires;
and
      (4)   The period of time in which the action is required to be
accomplished, measured from the time that the notice is given.
(Ord. 97-03, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 92.05 FAILURE TO COMPLY CREATES LIEN.
   Failure to comply with the judgment entered in this subchapter will result
in a lien filed on the tax duplicated against the property described. Written
notice of such action will be given to the property owner by certified mail.
(Ord. 96-06, passed 9-9-1996) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.06 PROVISIONS IN ADDITION TO OTHER APPLICABLE LAW.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall not be construed to be the exclusive
means of dealing with the regulation and control of housing and sanitation, and
with nuisances, but shall be a remedy provided in addition to the applicable
state statutes and other applicable laws.
(Ord. 93-08, passed 2-7-1993)
PUBLIC HEALTH NUISANCES
§ 92.20 AUTHORING OR MAINTAINING A NUISANCE UNLAWFUL.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, persons, company or corporation to
erect, construct, cause or permit, keep or maintain within the limits of the
town anything whatsoever which is injurious to health, or indecent, or
offensive to the senses of any of the inhabitants of said town, or any
obstruction to the free use of property by any such inhabitant, and any person
or persons maintaining any nuisance above referred to is thereby declared to be
the author and maintainer of a nuisance.
(Ord. 93, passed 7-14-1908) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   Any person who is in violation of §§
92.01 through
92.06 of this chapter who has been served with an order directed to them
pursuant to §
92.04 of this chapter, and who fails to take the required action within the
time period specified in the order, shall be guilty of a Class B infraction and
shall be subject to a fine not exceeding $1,000. The minimum fine for violation
of §§
92.01 through
92.06 shall be as follows:
      (1)   First offense: $100;
      (2)   Second offense: $250;
      (3)   Third offense: $500;
      (4)   Fourth offense: $1,000; and
      (5)   Each subsequent offense: $1,000.
   (C)   Any person or persons violating any of the provisions of §§
92.20 of this chapter, upon conviction thereof, except as otherwise provided,
shall be fined for each offense in any sum not less than $10 nor more than $50,
and be imprisoned for ten days, at the option of the court, and each day’s
violation shall constitute a separate offense.
(Ord. 93, passed 7-14-1908; Ord. 99-03, passed 6-17-1999)
